## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic constitutive laws and temperature affects material stiffness and flow behavior through thermal softening and thermally-activated mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Nonlinear elastic (power-law hardening): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (power-law stress-strain curve)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic hardening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T)**c3 (flow stress with thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally-activated softening with power-law hardening)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Temperature-dependent Voce: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturation hardening with thermal dependence)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (Taylor expansion of constitutive law)
- Thermal stress contribution: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T (combined mechanical and thermal stress)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally-activated deformation mechanism)
- Hyperbolic sine flow law (Sellars-Tegart): sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (high-temperature creep/flow)
- Ludwik-Hollomon with thermal factor: sigma = c0 * T**c1 * epsilon**c2 (power-law coupling of T and epsilon)
- Bilinear with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon) * (1 + c2 * T) (bilinear hardening with thermal factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 + c1*T) multiplying strain-dependent terms
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Thermally-activated mechanisms → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) factors representing Arrhenius-type temperature dependence
- Power-law hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 representing work hardening in metals (Hollomon relation)
- Competing elastic and plastic regimes → Sum of linear term (c0*epsilon) and nonlinear term (c1*epsilon**c2) representing elastic-plastic transition
- Stress-temperature product coupling → T**c1 * epsilon**c2 power-law coupling indicating temperature modifies the hardening exponent
- High-temperature creep regime → sinh or asinh functions of strain rate or strain, indicating transition between power-law and exponential creep
- Thermal expansion stress → Additive term proportional to T independent of strain, representing residual thermal stress

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*(T - c3)*log(epsilon + c4)
Candidate formulas: 54

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `90.776*epsilon**2 + 2.482*(T - 337.769)*log(epsilon + 1)`.

Expanding the GT: `90.776*epsilon**2 + 2.482*T*log(epsilon + 1) - 838.637*log(epsilon + 1)`.

So the GT has three structural components:
1. `epsilon**2` term
2. `T*log(epsilon + 1)` term
3. `log(epsilon + 1)` term

Let me check candidates that contain `log` terms and `epsilon**2` terms.

**Candidate 2**: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**2 + c2*exp(c3*epsilon) + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon**2 + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*epsilon) + 1) + c9`

Note: `log(c7*exp(c8*epsilon) + 1)`. When c7=1 and c8→0, this doesn't give log(epsilon+1). We need `log(exp(c8*epsilon) + 1)` which for small c8 ≈ log(1 + c8*epsilon + ...) but this isn't log(epsilon+1). No match.

**Candidate 54**: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**2 + c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon**2 + c4*log(c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + 1) + c7*epsilon/(c8 + epsilon)`

Same log structure - `log(c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + 1)` can't become `log(epsilon + 1)`.

**Candidate 33**: `T*c0*epsilon + T**c1*c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon**2*exp(c4/T) + c5*epsilon/(c6 + epsilon)`

No log terms. Can't match.

**Candidate 11**: `T*c0*epsilon + T**c1*c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon**2*exp(c4/T) + c5*sin(c6 + c7*log(c8*epsilon + 1))`

The sin term: `c5*sin(c6 + c7*log(c8*epsilon + 1))`. With c8=1, this is `c5*sin(c6 + c7*log(epsilon + 1))`. This is sinusoidal in log(epsilon+1), not linear. Can't match log(epsilon+1) directly.

**Candidate 9**: `T**(1/3)*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon + c2*sin(c3 + c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1)) + c6*epsilon**2*exp(c7/T)`

Same sin(log) structure. Can't produce a pure log term.

Let me reconsider candidates with explicit `log` in a linear (non-sin) form.

**Candidate 43**: `sqrt(T)*c0*epsilon**2/(c1 + epsilon) + sqrt(T)*c2*epsilon/(c1 + epsilon) + sqrt(T)*c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + c5*epsilon/(c1 + epsilon)`

This has `sqrt(T)*log(c4*epsilon + 1)` but needs `T*log(epsilon+1)`. Can't match since sqrt(T) ≠ T.

**Candidate 21**: `T*c0*epsilon**4/(c1+epsilon) + T*c2*epsilon**3/(c1+epsilon) + c3*epsilon/(c1+epsilon) + c4*epsilon*log(c5*exp(c6*epsilon)+1)/(c1+epsilon)`

The log term: `log(c5*exp(c6*epsilon)+1)`. For large c6*epsilon this ≈ c6*epsilon + log(c5). Not log(epsilon+1).

**Candidate 22**: Has `log(c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + 1)` terms with T multiplied. Setting c1=1, c6→0: `log(c5*1 + 1)` = constant. Not helpful.

After careful analysis, none of the candidates contain a term of the form `T*log(epsilon + 1)` or anything that can be algebraically manipulated to produce it. The `log(c*exp(c*epsilon)+1)` forms cannot become `log(epsilon+1)`, and `sin(c+c*log(epsilon+1))` cannot linearize to `log(epsilon+1)`. The `sqrt(T)*log` in candidate 43 can't become `T*log`.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match
